<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Education</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Transmission of knowledge and skills</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Education_(disambiguation)" title="Education (disambiguation)">Education (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p><b>Education</b> is a purposeful activity directed at achieving certain aims, such as transmitting <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> or fostering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skills" title="Skills">skills</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Character_trait" title="Character trait">character traits</a>. These aims may include the development of <a href="/wiki/Understanding" title="Understanding">understanding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rationality" title="Rationality">rationality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kindness" title="Kindness">kindness</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Honesty" title="Honesty">honesty</a>. Various researchers emphasize the role of <a href="/wiki/Critical_thinking" title="Critical thinking">critical thinking</a> in order to distinguish education from <a href="/wiki/Indoctrination" title="Indoctrination">indoctrination</a>. Some theorists require that education results in an improvement of the student while others prefer a value-neutral definition of the term. In a slightly different sense, education may also refer, not to the process, but to the product of this process: the <a href="/wiki/Mental_state" title="Mental state">mental states</a> and dispositions possessed by educated people. Education <a href="/wiki/History_of_education" title="History of education">originated</a> as the transmission of cultural heritage from one generation to the next. Today, <a href="/wiki/Educational_aims_and_objectives" title="Educational aims and objectives">educational goals</a> increasingly encompass new ideas such as the <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_education#Critical_theory" title="Philosophy of education">liberation of learners</a>, <a href="/wiki/21st_century_skills" title="21st century skills">skills needed for modern society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Empathy" title="Empathy">empathy</a>, and complex <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vocational_skills" title="Vocational skills">vocational skills</a>.
</p><p>Types of education are commonly divided into formal, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-formal_education" title="Non-formal education">non-formal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Informal_education" title="Informal education">informal education</a>. Formal education takes place in <a href="/wiki/School" title="School">education and training institutions</a>, is usually structured by curricular aims and objectives, and learning is typically guided by a <a href="/wiki/Teacher" title="Teacher">teacher</a>. In most regions, <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_education" title="Compulsory education">formal education is compulsory</a> up to a certain age and commonly divided into <a href="/wiki/Educational_stage" title="Educational stage">educational stages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary school</a> and <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a>. Nonformal education occurs as addition or alternative to formal education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> It may be structured according to educational arrangements, but in a more flexible manner, and usually takes place in community-based, workplace-based or civil society-based settings. Lastly, informal education occurs in daily life, in the family, any <a href="/wiki/Experience" title="Experience">experience</a> that has a formative effect on the way one thinks, feels, or acts may be considered educational, whether unintentional or <a href="/wiki/Autodidacticism" title="Autodidacticism">intentional</a>. In practice there is a continuum from the highly formalized to the highly informalized, and informal learning can occur in all three settings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> For instance, <a href="/wiki/Homeschooling" title="Homeschooling">homeschooling</a> can be classified as nonformal or informal, depending upon the structure.
</p><p>Regardless of setting, educational methods include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teaching" title="Teaching">teaching</a>, <a href="/wiki/Training" title="Training">training</a>, <a href="/wiki/Storytelling" title="Storytelling">storytelling</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discussion" title="Discussion">discussion</a>, and directed <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">research</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Methodology" title="Methodology">methodology</a> of teaching is called <i><a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">pedagogy</a></i>. Education is supported by a variety of different <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_education" title="Philosophy of education">philosophies</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Educational_science" title="Educational science">theories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Educational_research" title="Educational research">empirical research agendas</a>.
</p><p>There are movements for <a href="/wiki/Education_reform" title="Education reform">education reforms</a>, such as for improving quality and efficiency of education towards relevance in students' lives and efficient <a href="/wiki/Problem_solving" title="Problem solving">problem solving</a> in modern or future society at large, or for <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_education" title="Evidence-based education">evidence-based education methodologies</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Right_to_education" title="Right to education">right to education</a> has been recognized by some <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">governments</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[a]</a></sup> Global initiatives aim at achieving the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_4" title="Sustainable Development Goal 4">Sustainable Development Goal 4</a>, which promotes quality education for all.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Definitions_of_education" title="Definitions of education">Definitions of education</a></div>
<p>Numerous definitions of education have been suggested by theorists belonging to diverse fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall2006_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall2006-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matheson2014_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Matheson2014-6">[5]</a></sup> Many agree that education is a purposeful activity directed at achieving certain aims, especially the transmission of <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chazan2021_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chazan2021-7">[6]</a></sup> But they often include other aims as well, such as fostering skills and character traits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chazan2021_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chazan2021-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall2006_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall2006-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> However, there are deep disagreements about the exact nature of education besides these general characteristics. According to some conceptions, it is primarily a process that occurs during events like schooling, teaching, and learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peters1967_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peters1967-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericanHeritageDictionary_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmericanHeritageDictionary-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> Others understand it not as a process but as the achievement or product brought about by this process. On this view, education is what educated persons have, i.e. the <a href="/wiki/Mental_state" title="Mental state">mental states</a> and dispositions that are characteristic of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peters1967_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Peters1967-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericanHeritageDictionary_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-AmericanHeritageDictionary-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> However, the term may also refer to the academic study of the methods and processes taking place during teaching and learning, as well as the social institutions involved in these processes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericanHeritageDictionary_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-AmericanHeritageDictionary-10">[9]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etymologically" title="Etymologically">Etymologically</a>, the word "education" is derived from the Latin word <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:educatio#Latin" title="wikt:en:educatio">ēducātiō</a></i> ("A breeding, a bringing up, a rearing") from <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:educo#Latin" title="wikt:en:educo">ēducō</a></i> ("I educate, I train") which is related to the <a href="/wiki/Homonym" title="Homonym">homonym</a> <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:educo#Latin" title="wikt:en:educo">ēdūcō</a></i> ("I lead forth, I take out; I raise up, I erect") from <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:e-#Latin" title="wikt:en:e-">ē-</a></i> ("from, out of") and <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en:duco#Latin" title="wikt:en:duco">dūcō</a></i> ("I lead, I conduct").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some researchers, like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R._S._Peters" title="R. S. Peters">R. S. Peters</a>, have proposed precise definitions by spelling out the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Necessary_and_sufficient_conditions" title="Necessary and sufficient conditions">necessary and sufficient conditions</a> of education, for example: (1) it is concerned with the transmission of knowledge and understanding; (2) this transmission is worthwhile and (3) done in a morally appropriate manner in tune with the student's interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peters2015_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peters2015-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beckett2011_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beckett2011-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall2006_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall2006-4">[3]</a></sup> This and similar attempts are often successful at characterizing the most paradigmatic forms of education but have received numerous criticisms nonetheless, usually in the form of specific counterexamples for which the proposed criteria fail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beckett2011_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beckett2011-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peters1973_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peters1973-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> These difficulties have led various theorists to develop less precise conceptions based on <a href="/wiki/Family_resemblance" title="Family resemblance">family resemblance</a>. This means that all the different forms of education are <a href="/wiki/Similarity_(philosophy)" title="Similarity (philosophy)">similar</a> to each other even though they need not share an <a href="/wiki/Essence" title="Essence">essential set of features</a> characteristic of all of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall2006_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall2006-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordWittgenstein3.4_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordWittgenstein3.4-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> This view can also be combined with the idea that the meaning of the term "education" is context-dependent and may thus vary depending on the situation in which it is used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> Having a clear idea of what the term means is important for various issues: it is needed to identify and coherently talk about it as well as to determine how to achieve and measure it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson2003_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2003-17">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson2016_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Watson2016-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is disagreement in the academic literature on whether education is an <a href="/wiki/Axiology" title="Axiology">evaluative</a> concept. So-called <i>thick definitions</i> affirm this, for example, by holding that an improvement of the learner is a necessary requirement of education. However, different thick definitions may still disagree among themselves on what constitutes such an improvement. <i>Thin definitions</i>, on the other hand, try to give a value-neutral account of education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson2016_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Watson2016-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kotzee2011_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kotzee2011-20">[19]</a></sup> A closely related distinction is that between <i>descriptive</i> and <i>prescriptive conceptions</i>. Descriptive conceptions aim to describe how the term is actually used by regular speakers while prescriptive conceptions try to express what good education is or how it should be done.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chazan2021_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Chazan2021-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith2020_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith2020-21">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many thick and prescriptive conceptions base their account on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aims_of_education" title="Aims of education">aims of education</a>, i.e. regarding the goals that the activity of education tries to achieve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaPhilosophyOfEducation_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaPhilosophyOfEducation-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OxfordHandbookIntro_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-OxfordHandbookIntro-24">[23]</a></sup> These aims are sometimes categorized into <i>epistemic goods</i>, like knowledge and understanding, <i>skills</i>, like <a href="/wiki/Rationality" title="Rationality">rationality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Critical_thinking" title="Critical thinking">critical thinking</a>, and character traits, like <a href="/wiki/Kindness" title="Kindness">kindness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honesty" title="Honesty">honesty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watson2016_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Watson2016-18">[17]</a></sup> Some theorists focus on one overarching purpose of education and see the more specific aims as means to this end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haack1981_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haack1981-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation-23">[22]</a></sup> This can take the form of <a href="/wiki/Socialization" title="Socialization">socialization</a>, in which accumulated knowledge is transmitted from one generation to the next with the goal of helping the student function as a regular citizen in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chazan2021_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Chazan2021-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaEducation_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaEducation-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> More person-centered definitions focus on the <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">well-being</a> of the student instead: education is to help them lead a good life or the life they wish to lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chazan2021_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Chazan2021-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haack1981_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Haack1981-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> Various researchers emphasize critical thinking as an aim in order to distinguish education from <a href="/wiki/Indoctrination" title="Indoctrination">indoctrination</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OxfordHandbookIntro_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-OxfordHandbookIntro-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RoutledgeEducation_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-RoutledgeEducation-27">[26]</a></sup> This is motivated by the idea that mere indoctrination is only interested in instilling <a href="/wiki/Belief" title="Belief">beliefs</a> in the student without concern for their <a href="/wiki/Evidence" title="Evidence">evidential</a> status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaPhilosophyOfEducation_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaPhilosophyOfEducation-22">[21]</a></sup> Education, on the other hand, should also foster the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rational" title="Rational">rational</a> ability to critically reflect on those beliefs and question them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-28">[27]</a></sup> However, some theorists contend that certain forms of indoctrination may be necessary in the early stages of education until the child's <a href="/wiki/Mind" title="Mind">mind</a> is sufficiently developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordPhilosophyOfEducation-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Education can be characterized from the teacher's or the student's perspective. Teacher-centered definitions focus on the perspective and role of the teacher, for example, in the form of transmitting knowledge and skills while doing so in a <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">morally</a> appropriate manner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beckett2018_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beckett2018-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peters2015_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Peters2015-12">[11]</a></sup> Student-centered definitions, on the other hand, outline education based on the student's <a href="/wiki/Experience" title="Experience">experience</a> in the learning process, for example, based on how education transforms and enriches their subsequent experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beckett2011_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Beckett2011-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2011A_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson2011A-31">[30]</a></sup> However, conceptualizations taking both perspectives into account are also possible. This can take the form of describing the process as the shared experience of a common world that involves discovery as well as posing and <a href="/wiki/Problem_solving" title="Problem solving">solving problems</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beckett2011_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-Beckett2011-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beckett2018_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beckett2018-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Freire1970_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Freire1970-32">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span></h2>
<p>There are various ways how forms of education are commonly subdivided into different types. The most common subdivision is between formal, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-formal_education" title="Non-formal education">non-formal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Informal_education" title="Informal education">informal education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-La_Belle1982_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-La_Belle1982-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eshach2007_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eshach2007-34">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> However, some theorists only distinguish between formal and informal education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> A process of teaching constitutes formal education if it happens in a complex <a href="/wiki/Institution" title="Institution">institutionalized</a> framework. Such frameworks are usually chronologically and hierarchically organized as in modern schooling systems, which have different classes based on the student's age and progress, all the way from primary school to university. Because of its scale, formal education is usually controlled and guided by a <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">governmental</a> entity and is normally <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_education" title="Compulsory education">compulsory</a> up to a certain age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-La_Belle1982_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-La_Belle1982-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tudor2013_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tudor2013-37">[36]</a></sup> Non-formal and informal education differ from formal education due to their lack of such a governmental institutionalized framework. Non-formal education constitutes a middle ground in the sense that it is also organized, systematic, and carried out with a clear purpose in mind, such as <a href="/wiki/Tutoring" title="Tutoring">tutoring</a>, fitness classes, or the <a href="/wiki/Scouting" title="Scouting">scouting</a> movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-La_Belle1982_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-La_Belle1982-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tudor2013_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tudor2013-37">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> Informal education, on the other hand, happens in an unsystematic way through daily experiences and exposure to the environment. Unlike formal and non-formal education, there is usually no designated authority figure responsible for teaching.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eshach2007_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eshach2007-34">[33]</a></sup> Informal education is present in many different settings and happens throughout one's life, mostly in a spontaneous manner. This is how children usually learn their mother tongue from their parents or when learning how to prepare a certain dish by cooking together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-La_Belle1982_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-La_Belle1982-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tudor2013_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tudor2013-37">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-10"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup> Some accounts tie the difference between the three types mainly to the location where the learning takes place: in school for formal education, in places of the individual's day-to-day routine for informal education, and in other places occasionally visited for non-formal education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eshach2007_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-Eshach2007-34">[33]</a></sup> It has been argued that the <a href="/wiki/Motivation" title="Motivation">motivation</a> responsible for formal education is predominantly extrinsic, whereas it tends to be mainly intrinsic for non-formal and informal education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eshach2007_34-3"><a href="#cite_note-Eshach2007-34">[33]</a></sup> The distinction between the three types is normally clear for the paradigmatic cases but there are various intermediate forms of education that do not easily fall into one category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-La_Belle1982_33-4"><a href="#cite_note-La_Belle1982-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eshach2007_34-4"><a href="#cite_note-Eshach2007-34">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Formal education plays a central role in modern civilization. But in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primitive_culture" title="Primitive culture">primitive cultures</a>, most of the education happens not on the formal but on the informal level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaEducation_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaEducation-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scribner1973_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scribner1973-38">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> This usually means that there is no distinction between activities focused on education and other activities. Instead, the whole environment may be seen as a form of school and many or all adults may act as teachers. An important reason for moving to formal forms of education is due to the sheer quantity of knowledge to be passed on, which requires both a formal setting and well-trained teachers to be transmitted effectively. A side effect of the process of formalization is that the educational experience becomes more abstract and more removed from daily life. In this regard, more emphasis is put on grasping general patterns instead of observing and imitating particular behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaEducation_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaEducation-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scribner1973_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Scribner1973-38">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>Closely related to the distinction between formal and informal education is that between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conscious" title="Conscious">conscious</a> education, which is done with a clear <a href="/wiki/Intention" title="Intention">purpose</a> in mind, and unconscious education, which occurs on its own without being consciously planned or guided.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> This may happen in part through the <a href="/wiki/Personality" title="Personality">personality</a> of teachers and adults by having indirect effects on the development of the student's personality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> Another categorization depends on the age group of the learners and includes childhood education, adolescent education, adult education, and elderly education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> The distinction can also be based on the subject, encompassing fields like <a href="/wiki/Science_education" title="Science education">science education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Language_education" title="Language education">language education</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_education" title="Art education">art education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religious_education" title="Religious education">religious education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Physical_education" title="Physical education">physical education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> The educational methodology may be used as well for classifications, such as the difference between the traditional <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Teacher-centered_education&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Teacher-centered education (page does not exist)">teacher-centered education</a>, in which the teacher takes the center stage in providing students with information, in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Student-centered_learning" title="Student-centered learning">student-centered education</a>, in which students take on a more active and responsible role in shaping the classroom activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> The term "<a href="/wiki/Alternative_education" title="Alternative education">alternative education</a>" is sometimes used for a wide range of educational methods and approaches outside mainstream <a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">pedagogy</a>, for example, like the emphasis on narration and storytelling found in <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_education" title="Indigenous education">indigenous education</a> or <a href="/wiki/Autodidacticism" title="Autodidacticism">autodidacticism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Forms of education can also be categorized by the medium used, for example, as <a href="/wiki/Distance_education" title="Distance education">distance education</a>, like online education, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E-learning" title="E-learning">e-learning</a>, or <a href="/wiki/M-learning" title="M-learning">m-learning</a>, in contrast to regular classroom or onsite education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis2013_5-11"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis2013-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaEducation_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaEducation-26">[25]</a></sup> Various types of online education take the form of <a href="/wiki/Open_education" title="Open education">open education</a>, where the courses and materials are made available with a minimal amount of barriers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> Another classification is based on the social institution responsible for education and may include categories for institutions like family, school, civil society, state, and church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> When the term education is used in the sense of an achievement or a product, expressions like <i>type</i> or <i>level of education</i> refer to the person's academic or professional qualification, such as <a href="/wiki/High_school_diploma" title="High school diploma">high school completion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctor%27s_degree" title="Doctor's degree">doctor's degree</a>, or degrees in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vocational_training" title="Vocational training">vocational training</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal">Formal</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Formal learning" redirects here. For the subfield of formal epistemology and computer science, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Formal_learning_theory" title="Formal learning theory">Formal learning theory</a>.</div>
<p>Formal education occurs in a <a href="/wiki/Learning_environment" title="Learning environment">structured environment</a> whose explicit purpose is teaching <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">students</a>. Usually, formal education takes place in a <a href="/wiki/School" title="School">school</a> environment with <a href="/wiki/Classroom" title="Classroom">classrooms</a> of multiple students learning together with a trained, certified teacher of the subject.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> It can be subdivided into various categories or levels. The <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Classification_of_Education" title="International Standard Classification of Education">International Standard Classification of Education</a> (ISCED) was created by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as a statistical base to compare education systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup> In 1997, it defined seven levels of education and 25 fields, though the fields were later separated out to form a different project. The current version <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISCED" title="ISCED">ISCED 2011</a> has nine rather than seven levels, created by dividing the tertiary pre-doctorate level into three levels. It also extended the lowest level (ISCED 0) to cover a new sub-category of early childhood educational development programs, which target children below the age of three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_childhood">Early childhood</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_childhood_education" title="Early childhood education">Early childhood education</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg/220px-Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg/330px-Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg/440px-Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parent%27s_day_at_Eirfan%27s_Kindergarten.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Young children in a <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> in Japan</div></div></div>
<p>Education designed to support early development in preparation for participation in school and society. The programmes are designed for children below the age of three. This is ISCED level 01.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup> Preschools provide education from ages approximately three to seven, depending on the country when children enter <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary education</a>. The children now readily interact with their peers and the educator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup> These are also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursery_schools" title="Nursery schools">nursery schools</a> and as <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a>, except in the US, where the term <i>kindergarten</i> refers to the earliest levels of primary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> Kindergarten "provides a child-centred, preschool curriculum for three- to seven-year-old children that aim[s] at unfolding the child's physical, intellectual, and moral nature with balanced emphasis on each of them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> This is ISCED level 02.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary">Primary</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nepali_village_school_students.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2576" data-file-width="1932" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Nepali_village_school_students.jpg/170px-Nepali_village_school_students.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Nepali_village_school_students.jpg/255px-Nepali_village_school_students.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Nepali_village_school_students.jpg/340px-Nepali_village_school_students.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nepali_village_school_students.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nepali village school students</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">Primary education</a></div>
<p>This is ISCED level 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-4"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup> Primary (or elementary) education consists of the first four to seven years of formal, structured education. In general, primary education consists of six to eight years of schooling starting at the age of five to seven, although this varies between, and sometimes within, countries. Globally, in 2008, around 89% of children aged six to twelve were enrolled in primary education, and this proportion was rising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed. (September 2021)">full citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_For_All" title="Education For All">Education For All</a> programs driven by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, most countries have committed to achieving universal enrollment in primary education by 2015, and in many countries, it is compulsory. The division between primary and <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary education</a> is quite arbitrary, but it generally occurs at about eleven or twelve years of age. Some education systems have separate <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle schools</a>, with the transition to the final stage of secondary education taking place at around the age of fifteen. Schools that provide primary education, are mostly referred to as <i>primary schools </i>or <i>elementary schools</i>. Primary schools are often subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Infant_school" title="Infant school">infant schools</a> and <a href="/wiki/Junior_school" title="Junior school">junior schools</a>.
</p><p>In India, for example, <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_education#Variation_in_countries" title="Compulsory education">compulsory education</a> spans over twelve years, with eight years of elementary education, five years of primary schooling and three years of upper <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary schooling</a>. Various states in the republic of India provide 12 years of compulsory school education based on a national <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curriculum</a> framework designed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Educational_Research_and_Training" title="National Council of Educational Research and Training">National Council of Educational Research and Training</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary">Secondary</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Education%22" rel="nofollow">"Education"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Education%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Education%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Education%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Education%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Education%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">Secondary education</a></div>
<p>This covers the two ISCED levels, ISCED 2: Lower Secondary Education and ISCED 3: Upper Secondary Education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-5"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>In most contemporary educational systems of the world, secondary education comprises the formal education that occurs during <a href="/wiki/Adolescence" title="Adolescence">adolescence</a>. In the United States, Canada, and <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, primary and secondary education together are sometimes referred to as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%E2%80%9312_(education)" title="K–12 (education)">K-12</a> education, and in New Zealand Year 1–13 is used. The purpose of secondary education can be to give <a href="/wiki/Common_knowledge" title="Common knowledge">common knowledge</a>, to ensure literacy, to prepare for <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>, or to train directly in a <a href="/wiki/Profession" title="Profession">profession</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>Secondary education in the United States did not emerge until 1910, with the rise of large corporations and advancing technology in factories, which required <a href="/wiki/Skilled_worker" title="Skilled worker">skilled workers</a>. In order to meet this new job demand, <a href="/wiki/High_school_(North_America)" title="High school (North America)">high schools</a> were created, with a curriculum focused on practical job skills that would better prepare students for <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">white collar</a> or skilled <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar_worker" title="Blue-collar worker">blue collar</a> work. This proved beneficial for both employers and employees, since the improved human capital lowered costs for the employer, while skilled employees received higher wages.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Secondary education has a longer history in Europe, where grammar schools or academies date from as early as the 6th century, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[b]</a></sup> in the form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_education" title="Public education">public schools</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fee-paying_school" title="Fee-paying school">fee-paying schools</a>, or charitable educational foundations, which themselves date even further back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>It spans the period between the typically universal compulsory, <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary education</a> to the optional, selective <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary</a>, "postsecondary", or "<a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher</a>" education of ISCED 5 and 6 (e.g. <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a>), and the ISCED 4 <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">Further education</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">vocational school</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-6"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/220px-Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/330px-Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/440px-Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Calhan_High_School_Senior_Classroom_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A high-school senior (twelfth grade) classrooms in <a href="/wiki/Calhan,_Colorado" title="Calhan, Colorado">Calhan, Colorado</a>, United States</div></div></div>
<p>Depending on the system, schools for this period, or a part of it, may be called secondary or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high schools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasiums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyceum" title="Lyceum">lyceums</a>, middle schools, <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">colleges</a>, or vocational schools. The exact meaning of any of these terms varies from one system to another. The exact boundary between primary and <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary education</a> also varies from country to country and even within them but is generally around the seventh to the tenth year of schooling.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lower">Lower</span></h4>
<p>Programs at ISCED level 2, lower secondary education are usually organized around a more subject-oriented curriculum; differing from primary education. Teachers typically have
pedagogical training in the specific subjects and, more often than at ISCED level 1, a class of
students will have several teachers, each with specialized knowledge of the subjects they teach. Programmes at ISCED level 2, aim to lay the foundation for lifelong learning and human development upon introducing theoretical concepts across a broad range of subjects which can be developed in future stages. Some education systems may offer vocational education programs during ISCED level 2 providing skills relevant to employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-7"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper">Upper</span></h4>
<p>Programs at ISCED level 3, or upper secondary education, are typically designed to complete the secondary education process. They lead to skills relevant to employment and the skill necessary to engage in tertiary courses. They offer students more varied, specialized and in-depth instruction. They are more differentiated, with range of options and learning streams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED2011_57-8"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED2011-57">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">Community colleges</a> offer another option at this transitional stage of education. They provide nonresidential junior college courses to people living in a particular area.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary">Tertiary</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Education&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg/220px-Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg/330px-Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg/440px-Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Distributed_Intelligent_Systems_Department_laboratory.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Students in a laboratory, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_Polytechnical_University" title="Saint Petersburg State Polytechnical University">Saint Petersburg State Polytechnical University</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">Tertiary education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">Higher education</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">Adult education</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="373" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg/220px-Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg/330px-Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg/440px-Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_speaking_at_Peking_university.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Universities often host prominent guest speakers for student audiences, e.g. <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady of the United States</a> <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama" title="Michelle Obama">Michelle Obama</a> delivering remarks at <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, China</div></div></div>
<p>Higher education, also called tertiary, third stage, or postsecondary education, is the non-compulsory educational level that follows the completion of a school such as a high school or <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a>. Tertiary education is normally taken to include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Undergraduate" title="Undergraduate">undergraduate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">postgraduate education</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education and training</a>. Colleges and universities mainly provide tertiary education. Collectively, these are sometimes known as tertiary institutions. Individuals who complete tertiary education generally receive <a href="/wiki/Academic_certificate" title="Academic certificate">certificates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diploma" title="Diploma">diplomas</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">academic degrees</a>.
</p><p>The ISCED distinguishes four levels of tertiary education. ISCED 6 is equivalent to a first degree, ISCED 7 is equivalent to a masters or an advanced professional qualification and ISCED 8 is an advanced research qualification, usually concluding with the submission and defence of a substantive dissertation of publishable quality based on original research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED-65">[63]</a></sup> The category ISCED 5 is reserved for short-cycle courses of requiring degree level study.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED-65">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Higher education typically involves work towards a degree-level or <a href="/wiki/Foundation_degree" title="Foundation degree">foundation degree</a> qualification. In most developed countries, a high proportion of the population (up to 50%) now enter higher education at some time in their lives. Higher education is therefore very important to national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economies" title="Economies">economies</a>, both as a significant industry in its own right and as a source of trained and educated personnel for the rest of the economy.
</p><p>University education includes teaching, research, and social services activities, and it includes both the undergraduate level (sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary education</a>) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graduate_student" title="Graduate student">graduate</a> (or postgraduate) level (sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate school</a>). Some universities are composed of several colleges.
</p><p>One type of university education is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts">liberal arts</a> education, which can be defined as a "<a href="/wiki/College" title="College">college</a> or <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curriculum</a> aimed at imparting broad general knowledge and developing general intellectual capacities, in contrast to a professional, <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational</a>, or technical curriculum."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Although what is known today as liberal arts education began in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> the term "<a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts_college" title="Liberal arts college">liberal arts college</a>" is more commonly associated with institutions in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Williams_College" title="Williams College">Williams College</a> or <a href="/wiki/Barnard_College" title="Barnard College">Barnard College</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocational">Vocational</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="783" data-file-width="784" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg/220px-Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg/330px-Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg/440px-Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fotothek_df_n-10_0000828.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Carpentry is normally learned through <a href="/wiki/Apprenticeship" title="Apprenticeship">apprenticeship</a> with an experienced carpenter.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">Vocational education</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">Vocational education</a> is a form of education focused on direct and practical training for a specific trade or craft. Vocational education may come in the form of an <a href="/wiki/Apprenticeship" title="Apprenticeship">apprenticeship</a> or <a href="/wiki/Internship" title="Internship">internship</a> as well as institutions teaching courses such as <a href="/wiki/Carpentry" title="Carpentry">carpentry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_arts" title="The arts">the arts</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Post 16 education, <a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">adult education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> involve continued study, but a level no different from that found at upper secondary, and are grouped together as ISCED 4, post-secondary non-tertiary education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISCED_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-ISCED-65">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special">Special</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Special_education" title="Special education">Special education</a></div>
<p>In the past, those who were disabled were often not eligible for public education. Children with disabilities were repeatedly denied an education by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physicians" title="Physicians">physicians</a> or special tutors. These early physicians (people like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Itard" title="Itard">Itard</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard_S%C3%A9guin" title="Édouard Séguin">Seguin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Gridley_Howe" title="Samuel Gridley Howe">Howe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hopkins_Gallaudet" title="Thomas Hopkins Gallaudet">Gallaudet</a>) set the foundation for special education today. They focused on individualized instruction and functional skills. In its early years, special education was only provided to people with severe disabilities, but more recently it has been opened to anyone who has experienced difficulty learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Credo_Reference_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Credo_Reference-69">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Unconventional_forms">Unconventional forms</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative">Alternative</span></h3>
<div class="boilerplate metadata plainlinks tfd" id="tfd" style="background-color: transparent; padding: 0; font-size:xx-small; color:#000000; text-align: center; border-bottom:1px solid #AAAAAA; overflow:hidden;">‹ The <a href="/wiki/Help:Template" title="Help:Template">template</a> below (<i><a href="/wiki/Template:Globalize" title="Template:Globalize">Globalize</a></i>) is being considered for merging. See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Templates_for_discussion/Log/2022_October_6#Template:Globalize" title="Wikipedia:Templates for discussion/Log/2022 October 6">templates for discussion</a> to help reach a consensus. ›</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Globalize plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this section <b>deal primarily with US and do not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> You may <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Education&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a>, discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Education" title="Talk:Education">talk page</a>, or create a new section, as appropriate.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2020</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alternative_education" title="Alternative education">Alternative education</a></div>
<p>After the public school system was widely developed beginning in the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Alternative_education" title="Alternative education">alternative education</a> developed in part as a reaction to perceived limitations and failings of <a href="/wiki/Traditional_education" title="Traditional education">traditional education</a>. A broad range of educational approaches emerged, including <a href="/wiki/Alternative_school" title="Alternative school">alternative schools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autodidacticism" title="Autodidacticism">self learning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homeschooling" title="Homeschooling">homeschooling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Unschooling" title="Unschooling">unschooling</a>. Example <a href="/wiki/Alternative_school" title="Alternative school">alternative schools</a> include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montessori_method" title="Montessori method">Montessori schools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waldorf_education" title="Waldorf education">Waldorf schools</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Steiner" title="Rudolf Steiner">Steiner</a> schools), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Friends_Schools" title="List of Friends Schools">Friends schools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sands_School" title="Sands School">Sands School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Summerhill_School" title="Summerhill School">Summerhill School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walden%27s_Path" title="Walden's Path">Walden's Path</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Peepal_Grove_School" title="The Peepal Grove School">The Peepal Grove School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudbury_Valley_School" title="Sudbury Valley School">Sudbury Valley School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiddu_Krishnamurti" title="Jiddu Krishnamurti">Krishnamurti schools</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Open_classroom" title="Open classroom">open classroom</a> schools.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">Charter schools</a> are another example of alternative education, which have in the recent years grown in numbers in the US and gained greater importance in its public education system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>In time, some ideas from these experiments and paradigm challenges may be adopted as the norm in education, just as <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Fr%C3%B6bel" title="Friedrich Fröbel">Friedrich Fröbel</a>'s approach to <a href="/wiki/Early_childhood_education" title="Early childhood education">early childhood education</a> in 19th-century Germany has been incorporated into contemporary <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> classrooms. Other influential writers and thinkers have included the <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Swiss</a> <a href="/wiki/Humanitarianism" title="Humanitarianism">humanitarian</a> <a href="/wiki/Johann_Heinrich_Pestalozzi" title="Johann Heinrich Pestalozzi">Johann Heinrich Pestalozzi</a>; the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Transcendentalism" title="Transcendentalism">transcendentalists</a> <a href="/wiki/Amos_Bronson_Alcott" title="Amos Bronson Alcott">Amos Bronson Alcott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Ralph Waldo Emerson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Henry David Thoreau</a>; the founders of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Educational_progressivism" title="Educational progressivism">progressive education</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Dewey" title="John Dewey">John Dewey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Wayland_Parker" title="Francis Wayland Parker">Francis Parker</a>; and educational pioneers such as <a href="/wiki/Maria_Montessori" title="Maria Montessori">Maria Montessori</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Steiner" title="Rudolf Steiner">Rudolf Steiner</a>, and more recently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Caldwell_Holt" title="John Caldwell Holt">John Caldwell Holt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_Goodman_(writer)" title="Paul Goodman (writer)">Paul Goodman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Mayer" title="Frederick Mayer">Frederick Mayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Dennison" title="George Dennison">George Dennison</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Illich" title="Ivan Illich">Ivan Illich</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous">Indigenous</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schoolyard_essay2.JPG"><img alt="Na Schoolyard." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Schoolyard_essay2.JPG/220px-Schoolyard_essay2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Schoolyard_essay2.JPG/330px-Schoolyard_essay2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Schoolyard_essay2.JPG/440px-Schoolyard_essay2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schoolyard_essay2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_education" title="Indigenous education">Teaching indigenous knowledge</a>, models, and methods in <a href="/wiki/Yanyuan_County" title="Yanyuan County">Yanyuan County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a>, China</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_education" title="Indigenous education">Indigenous education</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_education" title="Indigenous education">Indigenous education</a> refers to the inclusion of indigenous knowledge, models, methods, and content within formal and non-formal educational systems. Often in a post-colonial context, the growing recognition and use of indigenous education methods can be a response to the erosion and loss of indigenous knowledge and language through the processes of colonialism. Furthermore, it can enable indigenous communities to "reclaim and revalue their languages and cultures, and in so doing, improve the educational success of indigenous students."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Informal_learning">Informal learning</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Informal_learning" title="Informal learning">Informal learning</a></div>
<p><b>Informal learning</b> is one of three forms of learning defined by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD). Informal learning occurs in a variety of places, such as at <a href="/wiki/Home" title="Home">home</a>, <a href="/wiki/Employment" title="Employment">work</a>, and through daily interactions and shared relationships among members of society. For many learners, this includes <a href="/wiki/Language_acquisition" title="Language acquisition">language acquisition</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_norm" title="Cultural norm">cultural norms</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manners" title="Manners">manners</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1131" data-file-width="1446" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg/220px-Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg/330px-Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg/440px-Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Khamla_Panyasouk_of_Big_Brother_Mouse_reads_to_children.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A volunteer reads aloud to children in <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In informal learning, there is often a reference person, a peer or expert, to guide the learner. If learners have a personal interest in what they are informally being taught, learners tend to expand their existing knowledge and conceive new ideas about the topic being learned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogoff_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rogoff-73">[71]</a></sup> For example, a museum is traditionally considered an informal learning environment, as there is room for free choice, a diverse and potentially non-standardized range of topics, flexible structures, socially rich interaction, and no externally imposed assessments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>While informal learning often takes place outside educational <a href="/wiki/School" title="School">establishments</a> and does not follow a specified curriculum, it can also occur within educational settings and even during formal learning situations. Educators can structure their lessons to directly utilize their students informal learning skills within the education setting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogoff_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rogoff-73">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 19th century, education through play began to be recognized as making an important contribution to <a href="/wiki/Child_development" title="Child development">child development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> In the early 20th century, the concept was broadened to include young adults but the emphasis was on physical activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L.P._Jacks" title="L.P. Jacks">L.P. Jacks</a>, also an early proponent of lifelong learning, described education through recreation: "A master in the art of living draws no sharp distinction between his work and his play, his labour, and his leisure, his mind and his body, his education and his recreation. He hardly knows which is which. He simply pursues his vision of excellence through whatever he is doing and leaves others to determine whether he is working or playing. To himself, he always seems to be doing both. Enough for him that he does it well."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> Education through recreation is the opportunity to learn in a seamless fashion through all of life's activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ullah_2012_165–170_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ullah_2012_165–170-78">[76]</a></sup> The concept has been revived by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario" title="University of Western Ontario">University of Western Ontario</a> to teach <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">anatomy</a> to medical students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ullah_2012_165–170_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ullah_2012_165–170-78">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-directed_learning">Self-directed learning</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autodidacticism" title="Autodidacticism">Autodidacticism</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Autodidacticism" title="Autodidacticism">Autodidacticism</a> (also autodidactism) is self-directed learning.
