One may become an autodidact at nearly any point in one's life. <a href="/wiki/List_of_autodidacts" title="List of autodidacts">Notable autodidacts</a> include <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> (U.S. president), <a href="/wiki/Srinivasa_Ramanujan" title="Srinivasa Ramanujan">Srinivasa Ramanujan</a> (mathematician), <a href="/wiki/Michael_Faraday" title="Michael Faraday">Michael Faraday</a> (chemist and physicist), <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> (naturalist), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Alva_Edison" title="Thomas Alva Edison">Thomas Alva Edison</a> (inventor), <a href="/wiki/Tadao_Ando" title="Tadao Ando">Tadao Ando</a> (architect), <a href="/wiki/George_Bernard_Shaw" title="George Bernard Shaw">George Bernard Shaw</a> (playwright), <a href="/wiki/Frank_Zappa" title="Frank Zappa">Frank Zappa</a> (composer, recording engineer, film director), and <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> (engineer, scientist, mathematician).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evidence-based">Evidence-based</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_education" title="Evidence-based education">Evidence-based education</a></div>
<p>Evidence-based education is the use of well designed scientific studies to determine which education methods work best. It consists of evidence-based teaching and evidence-based learning. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evidence-based_learning" title="Evidence-based learning">Evidence-based learning</a> methods such as <a href="/wiki/Spaced_repetition" title="Spaced repetition">spaced repetition</a> can increase rate of learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> The evidence-based education movement has its roots in the larger movement towards <a href="/wiki/Evidence-based_practice" title="Evidence-based practice">evidence-based-practices</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_learning_and_electronic_technology">Open learning and electronic technology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Open_education" title="Open education">Open education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Educational_technology" title="Educational technology">Educational technology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/220px-Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/330px-Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/440px-Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Children_computing_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Children computing by David Shankbone</div></div></div>
<p>Many large university institutions are now starting to offer free or almost free full courses, through open education, such as <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">Berkeley</a> teaming up to form <a href="/wiki/EdX" title="EdX">edX</a>. Other universities offering open education are prestigious private universities such as <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">Caltech</a>, as well as notable public universities including <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>.
</p><p>Open education has been called the biggest change in the way people learn since the printing press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> Despite favourable studies on effectiveness, many people may still desire to choose traditional campus education for social and cultural reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many open universities are working to have the ability to offer students standardized testing and traditional degrees and credentials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>The conventional merit-system degree is currently not as common in open education as it is in campus universities, although some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_universities" title="Open universities">open universities</a> do already offer conventional degrees such as the <a href="/wiki/Open_University" title="Open University">Open University</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. Presently, many of the major open education sources offer their own form of certificate.
</p><p>Out of 182 colleges surveyed in 2009 nearly half said tuition for online courses was higher than for campus-based ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2010 meta-analysis found that online and blended educational approaches had better outcomes than methods that used solely face-to-face interaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_schooling">Public schooling</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2120" data-file-width="3784" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg/220px-%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg/330px-%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg/440px-%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E5%8C%97%E5%B8%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%A5%BF%E9%97%A8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Beijing_Normal_University" title="Beijing Normal University">Beijing Normal University</a>, which is governed directly by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of Education of the People's Republic of China">Chinese Ministry of Education</a>, is an example of collaboration between different entities in the education sector.</div></div></div>
<p>The education sector or education system is a group of institutions (ministries of education, local educational authorities, teacher training institutions, schools, universities, etc.) whose primary purpose is to provide education to children and young people in educational settings. It involves a wide range of people (<a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curriculum</a> developers, inspectors, school principals, <a href="/wiki/Teacher" title="Teacher">teachers</a>, school nurses, students, etc.). These institutions can vary according to different contexts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-85">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>Schools deliver education, with support from the rest of the education system through various elements such as <a href="/wiki/Education_policy" title="Education policy">education policies</a> and guidelines – to which school policies can refer – curricula and learning materials, as well as pre- and in-service teacher training programmes. The school environment – both physical (infrastructures) and psychological (school climate) – is also guided by school policies that should ensure the well-being of students when they are in school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-:02-85">[83]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> has found that schools tend to perform best when principals have full authority and responsibility for ensuring that students are proficient in core subjects upon graduation. They must also seek feedback from students for quality-assurance and improvement. Governments should limit themselves to monitoring student proficiency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>The education sector is fully integrated into society, through interactions with numerous stakeholders and other sectors. These include parents, local communities, religious leaders, NGOs, stakeholders involved in health, <a href="/wiki/Child_protection" title="Child protection">child protection</a>, justice and law enforcement (police), media and political leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_85-2"><a href="#cite_note-:02-85">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>The shape, methodologies, taught material – the <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curriculum</a> – of formal education is decided by political decision makers along with federal agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/State_education_agency" title="State education agency">state education agency</a> in the United States.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_education" title="History of education">History of education</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medrese(school-mosque)-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1968" data-file-width="2749" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Medrese%28school-mosque%29-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg/220px-Medrese%28school-mosque%29-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Medrese%28school-mosque%29-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg/330px-Medrese%28school-mosque%29-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Medrese%28school-mosque%29-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg/440px-Medrese%28school-mosque%29-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medrese(school-mosque)-Old_City_Baku_Azerbaijan_1646.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Historical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrasah" title="Madrasah">Madrasah</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nalanda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1571" data-file-width="2209" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Nalanda.jpg/220px-Nalanda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Nalanda.jpg/330px-Nalanda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Nalanda.jpg/440px-Nalanda.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nalanda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nalanda" title="Nalanda">Nalanda</a>, ancient centre for higher learning</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1652" data-file-width="1614" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg/220px-Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg/330px-Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg/440px-Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plato%27s_Academy_mosaic_from_Pompeii.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a>'s academy, <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaic</a> from <a href="/wiki/Pompeii" title="Pompeii">Pompeii</a></div></div></div><p>
Education began in prehistory, as adults trained the young in the knowledge and skills deemed necessary in their society. In pre-<a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literate</a> societies, this was achieved orally and through imitation. Story-telling passed knowledge, values, and skills from one generation to the next. As cultures began to extend their <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> beyond skills that could be readily learned through imitation, formal education developed. Schools existed in Egypt at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Kingdom_of_Egypt" title="Middle Kingdom of Egypt">Middle Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAssmann2002127_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAssmann2002127-87">[85]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4988" data-file-width="3338" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg/170px-Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg/255px-Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg/340px-Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ricci_Guangqi_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Matteo_Ricci" title="Matteo Ricci">Matteo Ricci</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Xu_Guangqi" title="Xu Guangqi">Xu Guangqi</a> (right) in the Chinese edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Euclid%27s_Elements" title="Euclid's Elements">Euclid's Elements</a></i> published in 1607</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Platonic_Academy" title="Platonic Academy">Academy</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Athens" title="Ancient Athens">Athens</a>, the first institution of higher learning in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELynch197247_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELynch197247-88">[86]</a></sup> The city of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> in Egypt, established in 330 BCE, became the successor to Athens as the intellectual cradle of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>. There, the great <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Alexandria" title="Library of Alexandria">Library of Alexandria</a> was built in the 3rd century BCE. European civilizations suffered a collapse of literacy and organization following the fall of <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> in CE 476.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlainey2004?_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlainey2004?-89">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confucius" title="Confucius">Confucius</a> (551–479 BCE), of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Lu" title="State of Lu">State of Lu</a>, was the country's most influential ancient philosopher, whose educational outlook continues to influence the societies of China and neighbours like Korea, Japan, and Vietnam. Confucius gathered disciples and searched in vain for a ruler who would adopt his ideals for good governance, but his <a href="/wiki/Analects" title="Analects">Analects</a> were written down by followers and have continued to influence education in East Asia into the modern era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Aztecs had schools for the noble youths called <a href="/wiki/Calmecac" title="Calmecac">Calmecac</a> where they would receive rigorous religious and military training. The <a href="/wiki/Aztecs" title="Aztecs">Aztecs</a> also had a well-developed theory about education, which has an equivalent word in <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a> called <i>tlacahuapahualiztli.</i> It means "the art of raising or educating a person",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColin201465_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColin201465-91">[89]</a></sup> or "the art of strengthening or bringing up men".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeón-Portilla2012134–35_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeón-Portilla2012134–35-92">[90]</a></sup> This was a broad conceptualization of education, which prescribed that it begins at home, supported by formal schooling, and reinforced by community living. Historians cite that formal education was mandatory for everyone regardless of social class and gender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReagan2005108_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReagan2005108-93">[91]</a></sup> There was also the word <i>neixtlamachiliztli</i>, which is "the act of giving wisdom to the face."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeón-Portilla2012134–35_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeón-Portilla2012134–35-92">[90]</a></sup> These concepts underscore a complex set of educational practices, which was oriented towards communicating to the next generation the experience and intellectual heritage of the past for the purpose of individual development and his integration into the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeón-Portilla2012134–35_92-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeón-Portilla2012134–35-92">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_of_Rome" title="Fall of Rome">Fall of Rome</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> became the sole preserver of literate scholarship in Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> The church established <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_schools" title="Cathedral schools">cathedral schools</a> in the Early Middle Ages as centres of advanced education. Some of these establishments ultimately evolved into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_universities" title="Medieval universities">medieval universities</a> and forebears of many of Europe's modern universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlainey2004?_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlainey2004?-89">[87]</a></sup> During the High Middle Ages, <a href="/wiki/Chartres_Cathedral" title="Chartres Cathedral">Chartres Cathedral</a> operated the famous and influential <a href="/wiki/School_of_Chartres" title="School of Chartres">Chartres Cathedral School</a>. The medieval universities of Western Christendom were well-integrated across all of Western Europe, encouraged freedom of inquiry, and produced a great variety of fine scholars and natural philosophers, including <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Naples" title="University of Naples">University of Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Grosseteste" title="Robert Grosseteste">Robert Grosseteste</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, an early expositor of a systematic method of scientific experimentation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> and Saint <a href="/wiki/Albertus_Magnus" title="Albertus Magnus">Albert the Great</a>, a pioneer of biological field research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> Founded in 1088, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Bologne" title="University of Bologne">University of Bologne</a> is considered the first, and the oldest continually operating university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESanzBergan2006136_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESanzBergan2006136-97">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>Elsewhere during the Middle Ages, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_science" title="Islamic science">Islamic science</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mathematics_in_medieval_Islam" title="Mathematics in medieval Islam">mathematics</a> flourished under the Islamic <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">caliphate</a> which was established across the Middle East, extending from the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in the west to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus" title="Indus">Indus</a> in the east and to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Almoravid_Dynasty" title="Almoravid Dynasty">Almoravid Dynasty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> in the south.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Renaissance" title="The Renaissance">The Renaissance</a> in Europe ushered in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_revolution" title="Scientific revolution">new age of scientific and intellectual inquiry</a> and appreciation of ancient Greek and Roman civilizations. Around 1450, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">Johannes Gutenberg</a> developed a printing press, which allowed works of literature to spread more quickly. The European Age of Empires saw European ideas of education in philosophy, religion, arts and sciences spread out across the globe. Missionaries and scholars also brought back new ideas from other civilizations – as with the <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_China_missions" title="Jesuit China missions">Jesuit China missions</a> who played a significant role in the transmission of knowledge, science, and culture between China and Europe, translating works from Europe like <a href="/wiki/Euclid%27s_Elements" title="Euclid's Elements">Euclid's Elements</a> for Chinese scholars and the thoughts of <a href="/wiki/Confucius" title="Confucius">Confucius</a> for European audiences. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Enlightenment" title="The Enlightenment">The Enlightenment</a> saw the emergence of a more <a href="/wiki/Secular_education" title="Secular education">secular educational</a> outlook in Europe. Much of modern traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_education" title="Western education">Western</a> and Eastern education is based on the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_education_system" title="Prussian education system">Prussian education system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>In most countries today, full-time education, whether at school or <a href="/wiki/Homeschooling" title="Homeschooling">otherwise</a>, is compulsory for all children up to a certain age. Due to this the proliferation of compulsory education, combined with population growth, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> has calculated that in the next 30 years more people will receive formal education than in all of human history thus far.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_goals">Development goals</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1350" decoding="async" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG/220px-Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG/330px-Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG/440px-Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Education_index_UN_HDR_2007_2008.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World map indicating <a href="/wiki/Education_Index" title="Education Index">Education Index</a> (according to 2007/2008 <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>Joseph Chimombo pointed out education's role as a policy instrument, capable of instilling social change and economic advancement in developing countries by giving communities the opportunity to take control of their destinies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> The 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development, adopted by the United Nations (UN) General Assembly in September 2015, calls for a new vision to address the environmental, social and economic concerns facing the world today. The Agenda includes 17 <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> (SDGs), including <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_4" title="Sustainable Development Goal 4">SDG 4</a> on education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1909, the percentage of children in the developing world attending school has increased. Before then, a small minority of boys attended school. By the start of the twenty-first century, the majority of children in most regions of the world attended some form of school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[101]</a></sup> By 2016, over 91 percent of children are enrolled in formal primary schooling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">[101]</a></sup> However, a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Learning_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Learning crisis (page does not exist)">learning crisis</a> has emerged across the globe, due to the fact that a large proportion of students enrolled in school are not learning. A World Bank study found that "53 percent of children in low- and middle-income countries cannot read and understand a simple story by the end of primary school."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> While schooling has increased rapidly over the last few decades, learning has not followed suit.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Universal_Primary_Education" title="Universal Primary Education">Universal Primary Education</a> was one of the eight international <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>, towards which progress has been made in the past decade, though barriers still remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-105">[103]</a></sup> Securing charitable funding from prospective donors is one particularly persistent problem. Researchers at the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">Overseas Development Institute</a> have indicated that the main obstacles to funding for education include conflicting donor priorities, an immature aid architecture, and a lack of evidence and advocacy for the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-105">[103]</a></sup> Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> has identified <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">corruption</a> in the education sector as a major stumbling block to achieving Universal Primary Education in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> Furthermore, demand in the developing world for improved educational access is not as high as foreigners have expected. Indigenous governments are reluctant to take on the ongoing costs involved. There is also economic pressure from some parents, who prefer their children to earn money in the short term rather than work towards the long-term benefits of education.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>A study conducted by the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_International_Institute_for_Educational_Planning" title="UNESCO International Institute for Educational Planning">UNESCO International Institute for Educational Planning</a> indicates that stronger capacities in educational planning and management may have an important spill-over effect on the system as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-107">[105]</a></sup> Sustainable capacity development requires complex interventions at the institutional, organizational and individual levels that could be based on some foundational principles:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-107">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>national leadership and ownership should be the touchstone of any intervention;</li>
<li>strategies must be context relevant and context specific;</li>
<li>plans should employ an integrated set of complementary interventions, though implementation may need to proceed in steps;</li>
<li>partners should commit to a long-term investment in capacity development while working towards some short-term achievements;</li>
<li>outside intervention should be conditional on an impact assessment of national capacities at various levels;</li>
<li>a certain percentage of students should be removed for improvisation of academics (usually practiced in schools, after 10th grade).</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internationalisation">Internationalisation</span></h3>
<p>Nearly every country now has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_primary_education" title="Universal primary education">universal primary education</a>.
</p><p>Similarities – in systems or even in ideas – that schools share internationally have led to an increase in international student exchanges. The European <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Socrates-Erasmus Programme</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> facilitates exchanges across European universities. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soros_Foundation" title="Soros Foundation">Soros Foundation</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> provides many opportunities for students from central Asia and eastern Europe. Programs such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a> have contributed to the internationalization of education. The global campus online, led by American universities, allows free access to class materials and lecture files recorded during the actual classes.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_for_the_Evaluation_of_Educational_Achievement" title="International Association for the Evaluation of Educational Achievement">International Association for the Evaluation of Educational Achievement</a> objectively monitor and compare the proficiency of students from a wide range of different nations.
</p><p>The internationalization of education is sometimes equated by critics with the westernization of education. These critics say that the internationalization of education leads to the erosion of local education systems and indigenous values and norms, which are replaced with Western systems and cultural and ideological values and orientation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology_in_developing_countries">Technology in developing countries</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OLPC_Haiti.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/OLPC_Haiti.jpg/220px-OLPC_Haiti.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/OLPC_Haiti.jpg/330px-OLPC_Haiti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/OLPC_Haiti.jpg/440px-OLPC_Haiti.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OLPC_Haiti.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The OLPC laptop being introduced to children in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_and_technology" title="Education and technology">Education and technology</a></div>
<p>Technology plays an increasingly significant role in improving access to education for people living in impoverished areas and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>. However, lack of technological advancement is still causing barriers with regards to quality and access to education in developing countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> Charities like <a href="/wiki/One_Laptop_per_Child" title="One Laptop per Child">One Laptop per Child</a> are dedicated to providing infrastructures through which the disadvantaged may access educational materials.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/One_Laptop_per_Child" title="One Laptop per Child">OLPC foundation</a>, a group out of <a href="/wiki/MIT_Media_Lab" title="MIT Media Lab">MIT Media Lab</a> and supported by several major corporations, has a stated mission to develop a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/$100_laptop" title="$100 laptop">$100 laptop</a> for delivering <a href="/wiki/Educational_software" title="Educational software">educational software</a>. The laptops were widely available as of 2008. They are sold at cost or given away based on donations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Africa, the <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa's Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD) has launched an "<a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development_E-School_Program" title="New Partnership for Africa's Development E-School Program">e-school program</a>" to provide all 600,000 primary and high schools with computer equipment, learning materials and <a href="/wiki/Internet_access" title="Internet access">internet access</a> within 10 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> An International Development Agency project called nabuur.com,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> started with the support of former American President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, uses the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> to allow co-operation by individuals on issues of social development.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> is developing technologies that will bypass land-based <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">telephone</a> and Internet infrastructure to deliver <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distance_learning" title="Distance learning">distance learning</a> directly to its students. In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">Indian Space Research Organisation</a> launched <a href="/wiki/GSAT-3" title="GSAT-3">EDUSAT</a>, a communications satellite providing access to educational materials that can reach more of the country's population at a greatly reduced cost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding_in_developing_countries">Funding in developing countries</span></h3>
<p>A survey of literature of the research into low-cost private schools (LCPS) found that over a five-year period ending in July 2013, debate around LCPSs to achieving <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_for_All" title="Education for All">Education for All</a> (EFA) objectives was polarized and finding growing coverage in international policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup> The polarization was due to disputes around whether the schools are affordable for the poor, reach disadvantaged groups, provide quality education, support or undermine equality, and are financially sustainable. The report examined the main challenges encountered by development organizations which support LCPSs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup> Surveys suggest these types of schools are expanding across Africa and Asia. This success is attributed to excess demand. These surveys found concern for:
</p>
<ul><li>Equity: This concern is widely found in the literature, suggesting the growth in low-cost private schooling may be exacerbating or perpetuating already existing inequalities in developing countries, between urban and rural populations, lower- and higher-income families, and between girls and boys. The report findings suggest that girls may be under represented and that LCPS are reaching low-income families in smaller numbers than higher-income families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-2"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>Quality and educational outcomes: It is difficult to generalize about the quality of private schools. While most achieve better results than government counterparts, even after their social background is taken into account, some studies find the opposite. Quality in terms of levels of teacher absence, teaching activity, and pupil to teacher ratios in some countries are better in LCPSs than in government schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-3"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>Choice and affordability for the poor: Parents can choose private schools because of perceptions of better-quality teaching and facilities, and an English language instruction preference. Nevertheless, the concept of 'choice' does not apply in all contexts, or to all groups in society, partly because of limited affordability (which excludes most of the poorest) and other forms of exclusion, related to caste or social status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-4"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li>Cost-effectiveness and financial sustainability: There is evidence that private schools operate at low cost by keeping teacher salaries low, and their financial situation may be precarious where they are reliant on fees from low-income households.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-5"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The report showed some cases of successful voucher where there was an oversupply of quality private places and an efficient administrative authority and of subsidy programs. Evaluations of the effectiveness of international support to the sector are rare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-6"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup> Addressing regulatory ineffectiveness is a key challenge. Emerging approaches stress the importance of understanding the political economy of the market for LCPS, specifically how relationships of power and accountability between users, government, and private providers can produce better education outcomes for the poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eldis_116-7"><a href="#cite_note-eldis-116">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theory">Theory</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="522" data-file-width="542" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png/220px-FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png/330px-FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png/440px-FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FinnGerberBoydZaharias2005.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A class size experiment in the United States found that attending small classes for three or more years in the early grades increased <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high school</a> <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">graduation</a> rates of students from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_income" title="Low income">low income</a> families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finn_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-finn-117">[115]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Educational_theory" title="Educational theory">Educational theory</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pedagogy">Pedagogy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">Pedagogy</a></div>
<p>Pedagogy is often defined as the study or <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> of <a href="/wiki/Teaching_method" title="Teaching method">teaching methods</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Watkins1999_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Watkins1999-118">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup> It investigates how the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aims_of_education" title="Aims of education">aims of education</a>, like the transmission of <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> or fostering <a href="/wiki/Skill" title="Skill">skills</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Character_trait" title="Character trait">character traits</a>, can be realized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> It is particularly interested in the methods and practices used for teaching in regular schools and some researchers restrict it to this domain. But in a wider sense, it covers all types of education, including forms of teaching outside schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson2005_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson2005-122">[120]</a></sup> In this general sense, it explores how teachers can bring about <a href="/wiki/Experience" title="Experience">experiences</a> in learners to advance their <a href="/wiki/Understanding" title="Understanding">understanding</a> of the studied topic and how the learning itself takes place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>A great variety of pedagogical theories is discussed in the academic literature. Mental-discipline theories date back all the way to ancient Greek. They see education as a form of training to help the learner improve their intellectual capacities. They often start from a certain ideal of what educated people should be like and formulate their teaching methods accordingly. Naturalist theories assume that there is already an inborn natural tendency in children to develop in a certain way. The teaching process is then organized in such a manner as to ensure that these tendencies and potentials are fully actualized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-2"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-3"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Herbartianism" title="Herbartianism">Herbartianism</a> divides the educational process into different phases and investigates how to best realize each phase. The initial phase consists of preparation before the actual teaching happens. During the teaching itself, new ideas are first presented to the learner and then associated to ideas with which the learner is already familiar. In later phases, the understanding shifts to a more general level behind the specific instances and the ideas are then put into concrete practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaHerbartianism_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaHerbartianism-123">[121]</a></sup> According to the international consortium known as <i><a href="/wiki/Multiliteracy#The_New_London_Group" title="Multiliteracy">the New London Group</a></i>, there are four central components to pedagogy. In <i>situated practice</i>, learning takes place by practically engaging in real-life situations. <i>Overt instruction</i> is closer to classical forms of teaching and aims at helping the learner construct new knowledge based on their experiences and pre-existing knowledge. In <i>critical framing</i>, learners reflect on and critically analyze what they learned earlier. <i>Transformed practice</i> involves putting into practice what they learned previously, usually in new contexts and sometimes in the form of teaching others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewLondonGroup1996_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewLondonGroup1996-125">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>Various <a href="/wiki/Learning_theory_(education)" title="Learning theory (education)">learning theories</a> are also discussed in pedagogy. They try to understand how learning happens and propose teaching methods according to these findings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaLearning_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaLearning-126">[124]</a></sup> According to apperception or <a href="/wiki/Associationism" title="Associationism">association theories</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mind" title="Mind">mind</a> is initially a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blank_slate" title="Blank slate">blank slate</a> and learns about the world by forming <a href="/wiki/Association_(psychology)" title="Association (psychology)">associations</a> between ideas and experiences. Education tries to ensure that the right associations are formed. <a href="/wiki/Behaviorism" title="Behaviorism">Behaviorism</a> understands learning as a form of conditioning. This happens by presenting the learner with a stimulus, associating this stimulus with the desired response, and solidifying this <a href="/wiki/Stimulus%E2%80%93response_model" title="Stimulus–response model">stimulus-response pair</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-3"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-4"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaLearning_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaLearning-126">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are many specific teaching methods available. Which one is most efficient in a particular case depends on various factors, like the subject matter as well as the learner's age and competence level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-4"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-5"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup> For this reason, students are often organized by age, competence, specialization, and native language into different classes and grades to ensure a productive learning process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-5"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-6"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup> Different subjects frequently use very different approaches: for example, methods focusing on verbal learning are common in language education while mathematical education is about abstract and symbolic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thinking" title="Thinking">thinking</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Deductive_reasoning" title="Deductive reasoning">deductive reasoning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-6"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy2003_119-7"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy2003-119">[117]</a></sup> One central requirement for teaching methodologies is to make certain that the learner remains <a href="/wiki/Motivation" title="Motivation">motivated</a>, for example, because of interest and curiosity or through external rewards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-7"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> Another component of many teaching methodologies is to include some form of test or assessment to ensure that the learner is making progress and to change the chosen method if necessary. An important pedagogical aspect in many forms of modern education is that each particular lesson is part of a larger educational enterprise governed by a <a href="/wiki/Syllabus" title="Syllabus">syllabus</a>, often covering several months or years. A further pedagogical factor concerns the instructional media used, such as books, worksheets, and audio-visual recordings as well as computer-assisted instruction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel2020_120-8"><a href="#cite_note-Peel2020-120">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychology">Psychology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Educational_psychology" title="Educational psychology">Educational psychology</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Educational_psychology" title="Educational psychology">Educational psychology</a> is the study of how humans learn in educational settings, the effectiveness of educational interventions, the psychology of teaching, and the <a href="/wiki/Social_psychology" title="Social psychology">social psychology</a> of <a href="/wiki/School" title="School">schools</a> as <a href="/wiki/Organization" title="Organization">organizations</a>. The terms "educational psychology" and "school psychology" are often used interchangeably. Educational psychology is concerned with the processes of educational attainment in the general population and in sub-populations such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gifted" title="Gifted">gifted</a> children and those with specific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disabilities" title="Disabilities">disabilities</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg/220px-2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg/330px-2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg/440px-2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2013._%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%86%D0%BA_336.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Knowledge Day in <a href="/wiki/Donetsk" title="Donetsk">Donetsk</a>, Ukraine, 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Educational psychology can in part be understood through its relationship with other disciplines. It is informed primarily by <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>, bearing a relationship to that discipline analogous to the relationship between <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a>. Educational psychology, in turn, informs a wide range of specialties within educational studies, including <a href="/wiki/Instructional_design" title="Instructional design">instructional design</a>, <a href="/wiki/Educational_technology" title="Educational technology">educational technology</a>, curriculum development, <a href="/wiki/Organizational_learning" title="Organizational learning">organizational learning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Special_education" title="Special education">special education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classroom_management" title="Classroom management">classroom management</a>. Educational psychology both draws from and contributes to <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_science" title="Cognitive science">cognitive science</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Learning_sciences" title="Learning sciences">learning sciences</a>. In universities, departments of educational psychology are usually housed within faculties of education, possibly accounting for the lack of representation of educational psychology content in introductory psychology textbooks (Lucas, Blazek, &amp; Raley, 2006).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Intelligence">Intelligence</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_and_education" title="Intelligence and education">Intelligence and education</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Human_intelligence" title="Human intelligence">Intelligence</a> is an important factor in how the individual responds to education. Those who have higher scores of intelligence-metrics tend to perform better at school and go on to higher levels of education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> This effect is also observable in the opposite direction, in that education increases measurable intelligence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> Studies have shown that while educational attainment is important in predicting intelligence in later life, intelligence at 53 is more closely correlated to intelligence at 8 years old than to educational attainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Personal Development</b>
</p><p>Education can also be a useful tool in personal development. This can include activities such as learning new skills, creating a personal development plan (PDP), developing talents, creating human capital, developing spiritually, or improving self-knowledge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> Even the action of teaching others can help improve oneself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Learning_modalities">Learning modalities</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Learning_modalities" title="Learning modalities">Learning modalities</a></div>
<p>There has been much interest in learning modalities and styles over the last two decades. The most commonly employed learning modalities are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual" title="Visual">Visual</a>: learning based on observation and seeing what is being learned.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hearing_(sense)" title="Hearing (sense)">Auditory</a>: learning based on listening to instructions/information.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kinesthetic" title="Kinesthetic">Kinesthetic</a>: learning based on movement, e.g. hands-on work and engaging in activities.</li></ul>
<p>Other commonly employed modalities include <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">musical</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interpersonal" title="Interpersonal">interpersonal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Verbal_reasoning" title="Verbal reasoning">verbal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logical" title="Logical">logical</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intrapersonal" title="Intrapersonal">intrapersonal</a>.
</p><p>Dunn and Dunn<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> focused on identifying relevant stimuli that may influence learning and manipulating the school environment, at about the same time as <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Renzulli" title="Joseph Renzulli">Joseph Renzulli</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> recommended varying teaching strategies. <a href="/wiki/Howard_Gardner" title="Howard Gardner">Howard Gardner</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> identified a wide range of modalities in his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiple_Intelligences" title="Multiple Intelligences">Multiple Intelligences</a> theories. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myers-Briggs_Type_Indicator" title="Myers-Briggs Type Indicator">Myers-Briggs Type Indicator</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keirsey_Temperament_Sorter" title="Keirsey Temperament Sorter">Keirsey Temperament Sorter</a>, based on the works of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jung" title="Jung">Jung</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> focus on understanding how people's personality affects the way they interact personally, and how this affects the way individuals respond to each other within the learning environment. The work of <a href="/wiki/David_Kolb" title="David Kolb">David Kolb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Gregorc" title="Anthony Gregorc">Anthony Gregorc</a>'s Type Delineator<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> follows a similar but more simplified approach.
</p><p>Some theories propose that all individuals benefit from a variety of learning modalities, while others suggest that individuals may have preferred learning styles, learning more easily through visual or kinesthetic experiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> A consequence of the latter theory is that effective teaching should present a variety of teaching methods which cover all three learning modalities so that different students have equal opportunities to learn in a way that is effective for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> Guy Claxton has questioned the extent that <a href="/wiki/Learning_styles" title="Learning styles">learning styles</a> such as Visual, Auditory and Kinesthetic(VAK) are helpful, particularly as they can have a tendency to label children and therefore restrict learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-titleGuy_Claxton_speaking_on_What's_The_Point_of_School_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-titleGuy_Claxton_speaking_on_What's_The_Point_of_School-142">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> Recent research has argued, "there is no adequate evidence base to justify incorporating learning styles assessments into general educational practice."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Mind.2C_brain.2C_and_education"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mind,_brain,_and_education">Mind, brain, and education</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Educational_neuroscience" title="Educational neuroscience">Educational neuroscience</a> is an emerging <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">scientific</a> field that brings together researchers in <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">cognitive neuroscience</a>, <a href="/wiki/Developmental_cognitive_neuroscience" title="Developmental cognitive neuroscience">developmental cognitive neuroscience</a>, <a href="/wiki/Educational_psychology" title="Educational psychology">educational psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Educational_technology" title="Educational technology">educational technology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_theory" title="Education theory">education theory</a> and other related disciplines to explore the interactions between biological processes and education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnsariCoch_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-AnsariCoch-145">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CochAnsari_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-CochAnsari-146">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goswami2006_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goswami2006-147">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MeltzoffScience09_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-MeltzoffScience09-148">[146]</a></sup> Researchers in educational neuroscience investigate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neural" title="Neural">neural</a> mechanisms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reading_(process)" title="Reading (process)">reading</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goswami2006_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Goswami2006-147">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Numerical_cognition" title="Numerical cognition">numerical cognition</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnsariNRN08_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-AnsariNRN08-149">[147]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Attention" title="Attention">attention</a>, and their attendant difficulties including <a href="/wiki/Dyslexia" title="Dyslexia">dyslexia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCandlissNoble_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCandlissNoble-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GabrieliScience09_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-GabrieliScience09-151">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dyscalculia" title="Dyscalculia">dyscalculia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Price2007_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-Price2007-152">[150]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ADHD" title="ADHD">ADHD</a> as they relate to education. Several academic institutions around the world are beginning to devote resources to the establishment of educational neuroscience research.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philosophy">Philosophy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LockeEducation1693.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="214" decoding="async" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/LockeEducation1693.jpg/170px-LockeEducation1693.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/LockeEducation1693.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LockeEducation1693.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Locke" title="John Locke">John Locke</a>'s work <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Thoughts_Concerning_Education" title="Some Thoughts Concerning Education">Some Thoughts Concerning Education</a></i> was written in 1693 and still reflects traditional education priorities in the Western world.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_education" title="Philosophy of education">Philosophy of education</a></div>
<p>As an academic field, philosophy of education is "the philosophical study of education and its problems its central subject matter is education, and its methods are those of <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NoddingsPOE_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-NoddingsPOE-153">[151]</a></sup> "The philosophy of education may be either the philosophy of the process of education or the philosophy of the discipline of education. That is, it may be part of the discipline in the sense of being concerned with the aims, forms, methods, or results of the process of educating or being educated; or it may be metadisciplinary in the sense of being concerned with the concepts, aims, and methods of the discipline."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-POEE_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-POEE-154">[152]</a></sup> As such, it is both part of the field of education and a field of <a href="/wiki/Applied_philosophy" title="Applied philosophy">applied philosophy</a>, drawing from fields of <a href="/wiki/Metaphysics" title="Metaphysics">metaphysics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epistemology" title="Epistemology">epistemology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Axiology" title="Axiology">axiology</a> and the philosophical approaches (speculative, prescriptive or <a href="/wiki/Analytic_philosophy" title="Analytic philosophy">analytic</a>) to address questions in and about <a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">pedagogy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education_policy" title="Education policy">education policy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curriculum</a>, as well as the process of <a href="/wiki/Learning_theory_(education)" title="Learning theory (education)">learning</a>, to name a few.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> For example, it might study what constitutes upbringing and education, the values and norms revealed through upbringing and educational practices, the limits and legitimization of education as an academic discipline, and the relation between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_theory" title="Education theory">education theory</a> and practice.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Purpose">Purpose</span></h3>
<p>There is no broad consensus as to what education's chief aim or aims are or should be. Different places, and at different times, have used educational systems for different purposes. The <a href="/wiki/Prussian_education_system" title="Prussian education system">Prussian education system</a> in the 19th century, for example, wanted to turn boys and girls into adults who would serve the state's political goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some authors stress its value to the individual, emphasizing its potential for positively influencing students' personal development, promoting autonomy, forming a cultural identity or establishing a career or occupation. Other authors emphasize education's contributions to societal purposes, including good citizenship, shaping students into productive members of society, thereby promoting society's general economic development, and preserving cultural values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup>
</p><p>The purpose of education in a given time and place affects who is taught, what is taught, and how the education system behaves. For example, in the 21st century, many countries treat education as a <a href="/wiki/Positional_good" title="Positional good">positional good</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-159">[157]</a></sup> In this competitive approach, people want their own students to get a better education than other students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-159">[157]</a></sup> This approach can lead to unfair treatment of some students, especially those from disadvantaged or marginalized groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-159">[157]</a></sup> For example, in this system, a city's school system may draw school district boundaries so that nearly all the students in one school are from low-income families, and that nearly all the students in the neighboring schools come from more affluent families, even though concentrating low-income students in one school results in worse educational achievement for the entire school system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Curriculum">Curriculum</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">Curriculum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curriculum_theory" title="Curriculum theory">Curriculum theory</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_academic_disciplines" title="List of academic disciplines">List of academic disciplines</a></div>
<p>In formal education, a <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curriculum</a> is the set of courses and their content offered at a <a href="/wiki/School" title="School">school</a> or <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a>. As an idea, <b>curriculum</b> stems from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_course" title="Race course">race course</a></i>, referring to the course of <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/deed" title="wikt:deed">deeds</a> and experiences through which <a href="/wiki/Child" title="Child">children</a> grow to become mature <a href="/wiki/Adult" title="Adult">adults</a>. A curriculum is prescriptive and is based on a more general <a href="/wiki/Syllabus" title="Syllabus">syllabus</a> which merely specifies what topics must be understood and to what level to achieve a particular grade or standard.
</p><p>An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_academic_disciplines" title="List of academic disciplines">academic discipline</a> is a branch of knowledge which is formally taught, either at the university – or via some other such method. Each discipline usually has several sub-disciplines or branches, and distinguishing lines are often both arbitrary and ambiguous. Examples of broad areas of academic disciplines include the <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">natural sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Instruction">Instruction</span></h3>
<p>Instruction is the facilitation of another's learning. Instructors in primary and secondary institutions are often called <a href="/wiki/Teacher" title="Teacher">teachers</a>, and they direct the education of <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">students</a> and might draw on many <a href="/wiki/Course_(education)" title="Course (education)">subjects</a> like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reading_(process)" title="Reading (process)">reading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">writing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> and <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">history</a>. Instructors in post-secondary institutions might be called <a href="/wiki/Teacher" title="Teacher">teachers</a>, instructors, or <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professors</a>, depending on the type of institution; and they primarily teach only their specific discipline. Studies<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (October 2019)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup>from the United States suggest that the quality of teachers is the single most important factor affecting student performance, and that countries which score highly on international tests have multiple policies in place to ensure that the teachers they employ are as effective as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRS_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-WRS-162">[160]</a></sup> With the passing of NCLB in the United States (No Child Left Behind), teachers must be highly qualified.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economics_of_education" title="Economics of education">Economics of education</a></div>
<p>It has been argued that high rates of education are essential for countries to be able to achieve high levels of <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> Empirical analyses tend to support the theoretical prediction that poor countries should grow faster than rich countries because they can adopt cutting-edge technologies already tried and tested by rich countries. However, <a href="/wiki/Technology_transfer" title="Technology transfer">technology transfer</a> requires knowledgeable managers and engineers who are able to operate new machines or production practices borrowed from the leader in order to close the gap through imitation. Therefore, a country's ability to learn from the leader is a function of its stock of "<a href="/wiki/Human_capital" title="Human capital">human capital</a>". Recent study of the determinants of aggregate economic growth have stressed the importance of fundamental economic institutions<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> and the role of cognitive skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the level of the individual, there is a large literature, generally related to the work of <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Mincer" title="Jacob Mincer">Jacob Mincer</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> on how earnings are related to the schooling and other human capital. This work has motivated many studies, but is also controversial. The chief controversies revolve around how to interpret the impact of schooling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> Some students who have indicated a high potential for learning, by testing with a high <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">intelligence quotient</a>, may not achieve their full academic potential, due to financial difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p>Economists <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Bowles_(economist)" title="Samuel Bowles (economist)">Samuel Bowles</a> and Herbert Gintis argued in 1976 that there was a fundamental conflict in American schooling between the <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarian</a> goal of democratic participation and the inequalities implied by the continued profitability of capitalist production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h2>
