<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tabletunterricht_06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Tabletunterricht_06.jpg/220px-Tabletunterricht_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Tabletunterricht_06.jpg/330px-Tabletunterricht_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Tabletunterricht_06.jpg/440px-Tabletunterricht_06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tabletunterricht_06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Computer-supported group learning</div></div></div>
<p>The world is changing at an ever quickening rate, which means that a lot of knowledge becomes obsolete and inaccurate more quickly. The emphasis is therefore shifting to teaching the skills of learning: to picking up new knowledge quickly and in as agile a way as possible.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Finnish schools have begun to move away from the regular subject-focused curricula, introducing instead developments like phenomenon-based learning, where students study concepts like <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_education" title="Climate change education">climate change</a> instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> There are also active <a href="/wiki/Educational_interventions_for_first-generation_students" title="Educational interventions for first-generation students">educational interventions</a> to implement programs and paths specific to non-traditional students, such as <a href="/wiki/First-generation_college_students_in_the_United_States" title="First-generation college students in the United States">first generation students</a>.
</p><p>Education is also becoming<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2020)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> a commodity no longer reserved for children;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> adults need it too.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> Some governmental bodies, like the Finnish Innovation Fund Sitra in Finland, have proposed compulsory <a href="/wiki/Lifelong_learning" title="Lifelong learning">lifelong education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies found that <a href="/wiki/Automation" title="Automation">automation</a> is likely to eliminate nearly half the jobs in developed countries during roughly the next two decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup> Automation is therefore considered to be a major factor in a "race between education and technology".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> Automation technologies and their application may render certain currently taught skills and knowledge redundant while increasing the need for other curricula – such as material related to the application of automation. It has been argued that formal education is "teaching workers the wrong things, and that deep reform is essential to facilitate the development of digital knowledge and technical skills, as well as nonroutine cognitive and noncognitive (or "soft") skills"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> and that the formal <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a>-organized education system – which is built on the Industrial Revolution model and focuses on <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">IQ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Memorization" title="Memorization">memorization</a> is losing relevance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> FSchools were found rarely teach in forms of "learning by doing", and many children above a certain age "hate school" in terms of the material and subjects being taught, with much of it being a "waste of time" that gets forgotten quickly and is useless in modern society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> Moreover, the material currently being taught may not be taught in a highly time-efficient manner and analyzing educational issues over time and using relevant forms of student feedback in efficiency analysis were found to be important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup> Some research investigates how education can facilitate students' interest in topics – and jobs – that scientific research, data, economic players, financial markets, and other economic mechanisms consider important to contemporary and future human civilization and states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>Research and data indicate future environmental conditions will be "far more dangerous than currently believed", with a review concluding that the current <a href="/wiki/List_of_global_issues" title="List of global issues">challenges</a> that humanity faces are enormous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG-20210113-top-s_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-TG-20210113-top-s-187">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> The effective resolval of such challenges may require novel lesson plans tailored towards skills and knowledge found to be both required and reasonable to be taught at the respective age with the respective methodology despite novel technological computation and information retrieval technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_software" title="Mathematical software">mathematical software</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs additional references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">additional citation(s) needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Environmental_education" title="Environmental education">Environmental education</a> is not widely taught extensively or facilitated while being potentially important to the protection and generation of – often unquantified – <a href="/wiki/Value_(economics)" title="Value (economics)">economic value</a> such as clean air that agents of the economy can breathe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Education_economics#Education_as_an_investment" title="Education economics">Education is often considered to be a national investment</a> which may not always optimize for cost-efficiency while optimizing only in terms of contemporary economic value metrics or evaluations such as of <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> without consideration of economic values or priorizations beyond these tools such as minimized <a href="/wiki/Marine_pollution" title="Marine pollution">marine pollution</a> and maximized <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs additional references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">additional citation(s) needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Researchers found that there is a growing disconnect between humans and nature and that schools "are not properly preparing students to become the scientists of tomorrow".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.1126/science.aau3877_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-10.1126/science.aau3877-191">[189]</a></sup> They also find that <a href="/wiki/Rote_learning#Versus_critical_thinking" title="Rote learning">critical thought</a>, social responsibility, <a href="/wiki/Health_education" title="Health education">health</a> and safety are often neglected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.1126/science.aau3877_191-1"><a href="#cite_note-10.1126/science.aau3877-191">[189]</a></sup> According to UNESCO, "for a country to meet the basic needs of its people, the <a href="/wiki/Science_education" title="Science education">teaching of science</a> is a strategic imperative".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>One example of a skill not commonly taught in formal education systems around the world but increasingly critical to both the individuals' lives and modern society at large is <a href="/wiki/Digital_literacy" title="Digital literacy">digital</a> <a href="/wiki/Media_literacy" title="Media literacy">media literacy</a> – the ability to access, analyze, evaluate, create, and act using all forms of modern <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">ICTs</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> with scientists calling for inclusion of it in curricula as well as for adult education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies have shown that <a href="/wiki/Active_learning" title="Active learning">active learning</a> rarely applied in schools is highly efficacious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup> Studies found that <a href="/wiki/Massive_open_online_course" title="Massive open online course">massive open online courses</a> offer a pathway to employment that currently bypasses conventional universities and their degree programs while often being more relevant to contemporary economic activities and the students' interests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup> Such online courses are not commonly part of formal education but are typically both completed and selected entirely on behalf of the student, sometimes with the support of peers over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Online_forum" title="Online forum">online forums</a>. In contrast, <a href="/wiki/Blended_learning" title="Blended learning">blended learning</a> merges online education with forms of face‐to‐face communication and traditional class-based education in <a href="/wiki/Classroom" title="Classroom">classrooms</a>, revealing itself to have the general capacity for increasingly relevant, resource-efficient and effective approaches to education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup> Deploying, using, and managing various tools or platforms for education typically imply an increase in economic investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup> Expenses for education are often large with many calling for further increases. Potential policies for the development of international <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_and_open_source_software" title="Free and open source software">open source</a> <a href="/wiki/Educational_software" title="Educational software">educational software</a> using latest technologies may minimize costs, hardware requirements, problem-resolval efforts and deployment-times while increasing robustness, security and functional features of the software.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="COVID-19_pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_education" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on education">Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on education</a></div>
<p>Beginning in early 2020, the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> disrupted education systems throughout the world, affecting nearly 1.6 billion learners in more than 190 countries. Closures of schools and other learning spaces have impacted 94 percent of the world's student population, up to 99 percent in low and lower-middle income countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup> Many schools made alternative plans during the pandemic, leading to a variety of in-person, <a href="/wiki/Blended_learning" title="Blended learning">hybrid</a>, and online-only plans, which led to challenges for many students, teachers, and families including children with learning disabilities and those learning in a language that is not their native one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unlv.edu_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-unlv.edu-214">[212]</a></sup> As of 30 September 2020 there were 27 countries that had localized school closures. In the United States, an estimated 55.1 million students were forced to cease in-person instruction as of 10 April 2020. A switch to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virtual_learning" title="Virtual learning">virtual learning</a> experience is particularly challenging for families that cannot afford the proper technology, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laptops" title="Laptops">laptops</a>, <a href="/wiki/Printer_(computing)" title="Printer (computing)">printers</a>, or a reliable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internet_connection" title="Internet connection">Internet connection</a>. When schools close, parents are often asked to facilitate the learning of children at home and can struggle to perform this task. This is especially true for parents with limited education and resources. Students who require special education found it difficult to progress through the curriculum without tools and support that they require.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup> Polling suggests that schools that serve a majority of students of color are far less likely to have access to the technology needed for remote learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unlv.edu_214-1"><a href="#cite_note-unlv.edu-214">[212]</a></sup> Only 66% of Black households in the U.S. had home broadband service in 2019. Only 45% of Black Americans owned a <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop</a> or laptop computer in 2015. Without access to the internet or a computer, Black parents are at a disadvantage in educating their children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup> The mental health of students has been greatly impacted due to the pandemic. It is estimated that three in ten participating in school at home have had their emotional and mental health negatively impacted. Similarly, the social lives of students have also been upended and this has been detrimental to the health of students worldwide which has also negatively impacted educational quality. This will be an issue for years to come. COVID-19 has shone a light on opportunity gaps and it will be up to educators and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Policymakers" title="Policymakers">policymakers</a> to direct the necessary resources to mitigating them in the coming years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unlv.edu_214-2"><a href="#cite_note-unlv.edu-214">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
